  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_a2a8614b-f6b1-4993-9f99-9364d858c590'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

<span id="freeTextContainer16571154401059220150"><b>For the love of all that is good in the world, <i>please</i> let this be a belated April Fools prank.</b><br/><a href='http://photobucket.com/images/no%20gif' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>

  <span id="freeText16571154401059220150" style="display:none"><b>For the love of all that is good in the world, <i>please</i> let this be a belated April Fools prank.</b><br><a href="http://photobucket.com/images/no%20gif" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1397101176ra/9231122.gif" alt="no gif photo: no fe7da528.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>When Book #8 made its hellish appearance onto bookstore shelves, I was like, "Ok. This sucks. But hey - he named it <i>Nevermore</i>. Maybe this means he's finally realized that he should <i>never</i> make <i>more</i> books in this series after this one."<br><br>But no. James Patterson has decided to milk the money cow and make <i>another</i> book. With an even stupider title than its predecessor. <br><br><i>Maximum Ride Forever</i>.<br><br>Ah, no thanks. How about <i>Maximum Ride Never Again</i>? Or <i>Maximum Ride Forever Alone</i>?<br><br>Authors need to know when enough is enough. And this series plunged to its death <i>way</i> before <i>Nevermore</i> made our brains hurt with its over-the-top love triangle and poor excuse for a plot.<br><br>I used to love this series when it started. And now it's just some series that I used to know.<br><a href="http://photobucket.com/images/gotye%20gif" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">

</a><br><br>Sorry, Maximum Ride. But I'm ending this relationship whilst I still slightly respect you!</span>

<div id="review_1135350719" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1135350719" />
    <a title="Angelina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13903436-angelina"><img alt="Angelina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1369166993p2/13903436.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1135350719?book_show_action=true">Dec 18, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Angelina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Angelina" href="/user/show/13903436-angelina">Angelina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13903436-angelina?shelf=adventure">adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13903436-angelina?shelf=trash">trash</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13903436-angelina?shelf=toilet-paper">toilet-paper</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1135350719" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15138396565692339482">JAMES PATTERSON, Come ON.<br/><br/>This is the last time, I swear, this is one time too many now. You said that Nevermore was the LAST BOOK and yOU ENDED IT WITH THE WORLD ENDING.<br/><br/>With the amount of times you wrenched Ari from his grave, the endless jerking around of Max and Fang, the constant mystery and secrecy about the Voice, I would’ve thought that Nevermore was enough for you. You could finally put a close to the series after trying to end it no less than twice. But no, you drug Maximum Ride out of h</span>
  <span id="freeText15138396565692339482" style="display:none">JAMES PATTERSON, Come ON.<br /><br />This is the last time, I swear, this is one time too many now. You said that Nevermore was the LAST BOOK and yOU ENDED IT WITH THE WORLD ENDING.<br /><br />With the amount of times you wrenched Ari from his grave, the endless jerking around of Max and Fang, the constant mystery and secrecy about the Voice, I would’ve thought that Nevermore was enough for you. You could finally put a close to the series after trying to end it no less than twice. But no, you drug Maximum Ride out of her grave for ten more years than you should’ve. You should’ve let it die.<br /><br />Because you killed it.<br /><br />I don't want to read about this Max, who cares so much about herself that she'd let the world die. I don't want to read about Fang, who abandoned Max as well as the new friends he made. I don't want to read a book just so I can see two lines mentioning the character I used to love so much, but bastardizing them into two-dimensional cutout of their former selves. <br /><br />Max and Fang were my first OTP. I loved them. I loved her. I loved how brave she was. I loved them so much.<br /><br />But then everything changed.<br /><br />Relegating your main cast to cameos, trivializing your narrator, bringing in new characters for no reason and tossing in a needless love triangle aren’t things a good writer does. But you don't write your books anymore, do you?<br /><br />How many lines did Nudge get in your last book? When’s the last time Gazzy did something important? Angel constantly being evil broke me. You used the same plot devices, the same cliched story lines. The last few books read worse than any other book I’ve ever read.<br /><br />And now Marvel’s making an adaptation of your books. You don’t deserve that. You’re sticking it to your manga (your beautifully drawn manga) and you’re trying to make as much money as possible.<br /><br />I know money means a lot to you, but Max meant a lot to me.<br /><br />She meant so much and I’m so tired of being pulled into your books just to have a amateur try to tell me a story. You don’t even write your own books anymore. I don’t know why I even try. I will not be reading this book. I wish I'd never read Nevermore. Sometimes, when I'm not twisted up in rage over your schemes, I even regret ever picking up this series. <br /><br />Once, these books meant the world to me. Once, I waited for them at the library for weeks and waited to buy them at the store. Not anymore. <br /><br />Thanks for making me hate something I used to love so much.<br /><br />- - -<br /><br />If Max were real and she was here, we both know what she'd say. <br /><br />But then again, I don't think you care anyways. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15138396565692339482" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1099061709" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1099061709" />
    <a title="Will M." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/20408288-will-m"><img alt="Will M." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1452951660p2/20408288.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1099061709?book_show_action=true">Nov 06, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Will M." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Will M." href="/user/show/20408288-will-m">Will M.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20408288-will-m?shelf=2015">2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20408288-will-m?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20408288-will-m?shelf=ya-sci-fi-dystopia">ya-sci-fi-dystopia</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1099061709" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2048570768580621478">Aside from the Harry Potter series, Maximum Ride was the series that I grew up with. Alongside HP, both helped me become addicted to reading. Without the two series, I don't think I'll be a reader. I have to thank Rowling and Patterson for making my reading experience as a child wonderful. I do hope though that this is really the final book of the series. Don't stretch it out further, Patterson. You finally gave the series proper closure, don't ruin that.<br/><br/>After the awful eight book, Nevermore, Pa</span>
  <span id="freeText2048570768580621478" style="display:none">Aside from the Harry Potter series, Maximum Ride was the series that I grew up with. Alongside HP, both helped me become addicted to reading. Without the two series, I don't think I'll be a reader. I have to thank Rowling and Patterson for making my reading experience as a child wonderful. I do hope though that this is really the final book of the series. Don't stretch it out further, Patterson. You finally gave the series proper closure, don't ruin that.<br /><br />After the awful eight book, Nevermore, Patterson decided to write an encore novel. I'm not sure if he read those hate-filled reviews for the supposed conclusion novel, but I'm among the ones who hated the way he ended it the first time. It was a slap in the face to end it the way he did. This novel though, it finally gave respect to the series that I've been reading ever since my early years. I'm honestly satisfied with this. The last part was a bit cheesy, but it was still what I wanted. Bottomline is, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Maximum finally saved the world, or at least what's left of it.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Less action packed as compared to some novels in the series. There were a lot of detours talking about the character's feelings rather than action scenes. I'm not complaining that much though because the character development further flourished. The plot was good despite the lack of action.<br /><br />Considering this is the last book of the series, I'm not going to talk about the character development anymore. If you've reached this far, then you know that the characters are really good. Max changed a lot from the first few books in the series, but not in a bad way I guess. Either she matured, or I did. Reading taste tends to change over the years.<br /><br />4/5 stars. Not the perfect book, but I'm sure I would've rated this 5 stars if I read it when I was a lot younger. My taste changed over the years, and lately I don't really enjoy YA anymore. Patterson is one of my favorite authors, and I can say that I see his writing here. I'm not sure if this is one of his books where he has a ghost writer, but hopefully not. Hopefully he started and ended the series. I can't recommend the series to adults, because obviously the targeted audience was young adults. I was around 13 or 14 when I started reading the series, so that's the reason why I loved this so much. If you're in your 20s, you'll probably not enjoy the series that much, but give it a try if you want. Thank you Patterson, for this really good series. There were a lot of bumps in the road, but the important thing is that I'm satisfied in the end. You managed to make one fan really happy.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2048570768580621478" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1289389787" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1289389787" />
    <a title="Xanith Hart" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19487032-xanith-hart"><img alt="Xanith Hart" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1398126497p2/19487032.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1289389787?book_show_action=true">May 25, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Xanith Hart" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Xanith Hart" href="/user/show/19487032-xanith-hart">Xanith Hart</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Not to the target age group</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19487032-xanith-hart?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19487032-xanith-hart?shelf=2015-books">2015-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1289389787" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9133429559491822705">Sorry not sorry, but I'm not okay with the book at all. JP seems to think for some reason that what he did was okay and it wasn't. Max was strong, independent and time after time she proved that she didn't need someone to save her. As an 11 year old starting this series I really looked up to her. She was the first book heroin that ever stood at to me as special. She reflected the type of strong I wanted to be. Around book six it had really begun to fade, but that was not the biggest deal, becaus</span>
  <span id="freeText9133429559491822705" style="display:none">Sorry not sorry, but I'm not okay with the book at all. JP seems to think for some reason that what he did was okay and it wasn't. Max was strong, independent and time after time she proved that she didn't need someone to save her. As an 11 year old starting this series I really looked up to her. She was the first book heroin that ever stood at to me as special. She reflected the type of strong I wanted to be. Around book six it had really begun to fade, but that was not the biggest deal, because she was still her. She was still strong and she was still Max. But by this book she was not Max. She was an entirely different person, who was no longer recognizable as the girl I had looked up to. And then for some reason JP felt the need to make her pregnant. <br /><br /><br /><br />That just isn't okay. She is a 15 year old girl, who has adamantly been against having children due to the fact that her life has been lived on the run. She had acknowledged that her situation was not ideal for having a baby, given the fact that she was constantly threatened. Max having a baby at 15 just shows how much JP disregards that girl he first wrote about, maybe even cared about. And the fact that they used it for an ad to draw people in just makes it worse. Having a 15 year old have a baby is not an acceptable plot device in this case. <br /><br /><br /><br />JP seems to have forgotten who he was writing for (or his ghost writer forgot). As a 17 year old finishing the series I have to say that I found it horrifying, whereas 11 year old me would have found it cute, when it isn't. How JP wrote at the end made it seem like Max was no longer a person. Suddenly she and this baby were jumbled together, neither with their own identities. I didn't needed a happy ending, but I also didn't need one where an author chooses to step over the line just to make more money.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9133429559491822705" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1021090174" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1021090174" />
    <a title="Brittany" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4763200-brittany"><img alt="Brittany" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1572102183p2/4763200.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1021090174?book_show_action=true">Aug 08, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brittany" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brittany" href="/user/show/4763200-brittany">Brittany</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4763200-brittany?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4763200-brittany?shelf=favorite-series">favorite-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4763200-brittany?shelf=amazing-ending">amazing-ending</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1021090174" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14114296615734148890">Before I read this I do want to put my own opinion out there. I do not like or agree with anyone posting one star or even a five star review of a book they haven't even read. It can go either way. This could be the best book or the worst book you ever read and already you're criticizing it. I'm indifferent to a ninth book to the series. I did enjoy the eighth book and was fine with it ending the way it did. At the same time I wanna know what the end of the world looks like and who all truly live</span>
  <span id="freeText14114296615734148890" style="display:none">Before I read this I do want to put my own opinion out there. I do not like or agree with anyone posting one star or even a five star review of a book they haven't even read. It can go either way. This could be the best book or the worst book you ever read and already you're criticizing it. I'm indifferent to a ninth book to the series. I did enjoy the eighth book and was fine with it ending the way it did. At the same time I wanna know what the end of the world looks like and who all truly lived through it's demise. If Patterson wants to have a ninth book that's his decision. He originally started Maximum Ride and Daniel X for his son and maybe his son asked for a ninth book. But of course some people aren't as big of a fan or not a fan at all of Patterson to know this so there you go. Maybe it isn't all about the money. Maybe Patterson has family who value his work and want to see more of a certain series so Patterson in return cares enough to have another book. He's not the only author who has said "this is the last book" and then changed his mind. Author's do it all the time and sometimes it's really NOT for money reasons. If they feel their story wasn't finished then that's really up to them not you. I will admit this is my favorite series I do hope the ninth book is better than the last. <br />UPDATE FULL REVIEW<br />James Patterson has brought to us yet another wonderful edition to the Maximum Ride series. This book was the absolute perfect way to end the series. Nevermore left many holes and I know many people including myself were a little disappointed with the turn out. It was a good book, but it didn't feel right to end the series with that book. Maximum Ride brought back all the same emotions from when I read all the other books as a teenager. I laughed, I cried (privately), and my heart broke and got pieced back together again and again. There was something in the book that I normally wouldn't agree with happening, but I couldn't help, but to get extremely excited and giddy. I'm happy that I stuck up for Patterson when many others are saying that the series was dead. No! Only the author gets to decide that, not the fans. Haters really need to just back up because this book was incredible! I know many dropped the series after the third book and I feel sorry for them because they have no idea what they're missing. Maximum Ride is such a raw and emotional series that certainly has taken me on the ride of my life. I love how I can try and predict what Patterson will do, but as usual I couldn't. Above all, I finished this book in a matter of hours! I did not want to put it down. I completely fell in love all over again and it has actually made me want to reread the series all over again. I don't think there will ever be a series that will take the place of Maximum Ride for me. But I do finally feel like the series has ended where it needs to. I actually feel like Patterson just may do a spin off on a certain new character. I would love that! It might not happen, but hey I can always dream can't I? This book was just like any other in the series. It was full of twists and so many surprises. This book was such a beautiful creation and it's meant to be the last. It's weird how I can look back and think that Nevermore really was not the end. At the time I was fine with the ending, but not completely satisfied. I was just happy that everything seemed to be somewhat of a happily ever after. But this book finally completed the beloved Maximum Ride adventures that I will forever hold within my heart. It's amazing that this book reminded me of how much I loved the series and of course still do. Maximum Ride has taken me on a journey like no book ever has before. Being a part of this series since I was fourteen and never stopped loving it. So many unanswered questions were filled and it truly feels like we can close the book on Maximum Ride. The ending was so bittersweet, but that's what probably made me love the last book the most. Bittersweet endings are a favorite of mine and this one was heart breaking yet it fell perfectly into place like a missing puzzle piece the series needed to finally be the end. Everything happens for a reason and I'm so happy that this book was brought to life. Thank you, Patterson for bringing my favorite series back to life and killing it again. This was truly beautiful. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14114296615734148890" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

There's a reason why I stuck to the Fax ship from the beginning, people. :) <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>I imagine some people won't like the way this story reverts to some of the infamous old Max Ride standbys - such as retconning character deaths, Angel being Angel (seriously, she's become way too creepy), and Dylan being Dylan (go away, winged smarmosaur.) But it wouldn't be a proper Max Ride swan song if it weren't done in the old style, would it?<br><br>Three years without answers, and now we finally have them. And the future looks a hell of a lot brighter for our beloved Flock now...a future that we can hopefully be free to imagine without the aid of another book. (Not that I wouldn't like another one, but let's face it, nothing lasts forever.)<br><br>So, hopefully, this'll be the only time I have to say this: <i>ave atque vale,</i> Max Ride and the Flock! :D</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1301353637?book_show_action=true">Jun 07, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aimee ~is busy sleeping~" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aimee ~is busy sleeping~" href="/user/show/29836931-aimee-is-busy-sleeping">Aimee ~is busy sleeping~</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29836931-aimee-is-busy-sleeping?shelf=1-2stars">1-2stars</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1301353637" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15532061475063186036">I remember how absolutely obsessed I was with this series, since middle school. They were such fun and everyone in the flock had their own funny and loveable personalities. From Toto the talking dog to troublemakers Gazzy and Izzy. And Max and Fang were my OTP. I joined a huge online forum for the book series and was on it every day. <br/>Then after the Final Warning, the series turned into utter crap. The whole "Max is special she's gonna save the world" repeated by everyone book after book without </span>
  <span id="freeText15532061475063186036" style="display:none">I remember how absolutely obsessed I was with this series, since middle school. They were such fun and everyone in the flock had their own funny and loveable personalities. From Toto the talking dog to troublemakers Gazzy and Izzy. And Max and Fang were my OTP. I joined a huge online forum for the book series and was on it every day. <br />Then after the Final Warning, the series turned into utter crap. The whole "Max is special she's gonna save the world" repeated by everyone book after book without Max actually saving the world or doing much got tired real fast. Everyone else in the flock got less and less page time each book and new, wholly uninteresting characters became the focus. The stupid nonsensical love triangle. The nice slow building relationship between Max and Fang reached high school drama and angst proportions. The dialogue became laughable and I'm pretty sure there was a ghostwriter. Plus, Ari must've died and came back alive more than 6 times by now. <br />Angel became such a weird, freaky little kid. Jeb kept turning from good guy to bad guy. Everyone just started becoming a caricature of themselves.<br /> <br />I was surpised to see this book because I thought the previous one was the last. Read it just for fun and the dialogue and writing felt really, really amateur-ish. I lost count of how many times by now Fang has left the flock out of some self-sacrificing ideals. And how many times by now Max burst into tears every time Fang or someone in the flock <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ "died"  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> only for it to be a false alarm. Plus, surprise, surprise....friggin Jeb again =_=. And the epilogue...cringe. <br />Well. I'll always remember my love for the first three books.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15532061475063186036" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1194024704" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1194024704" />
    <a title="- ̗̀ ash  ̖́-" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23051860---ash--"><img alt="- ̗̀ ash  ̖́-" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1503862776p2/23051860.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1194024704?book_show_action=true">Feb 07, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="- ̗̀ ash  ̖́-" class="user" itemprop="url" name="- ̗̀ ash  ̖́-" href="/user/show/23051860---ash--">- ̗̀ ash  ̖́-</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23051860---ash--?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23051860---ash--?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23051860---ash--?shelf=disappointing-ending">disappointing-ending</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23051860---ash--?shelf=problematic">problematic</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1194024704" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15351347102725648297">So lets start with... I'm glad that James Patterson wrote this book. My opinions about it does not change the fact that so many problems left with Nevermore were resolved as well as they could be in this book. But still... I just didn't like it. I only read this book because I was a loyal Maximum Ride fan, and I basically grew up with it in my childhood. Now that I'm older with more reading experience, all I can see are immense problems with this series. Maybe it's just me... but I don't know.<br/>To</span>
  <span id="freeText15351347102725648297" style="display:none">So lets start with... I'm glad that James Patterson wrote this book. My opinions about it does not change the fact that so many problems left with Nevermore were resolved as well as they could be in this book. But still... I just didn't like it. I only read this book because I was a loyal Maximum Ride fan, and I basically grew up with it in my childhood. Now that I'm older with more reading experience, all I can see are immense problems with this series. Maybe it's just me... but I don't know.<br>To be honest, this book/series was a mess... if you really read it and notice the details. I feel like the plot of this book was thought of overnight, and James Patterson decided to put 400 pages in one sitting. While I was reading it all I could think was, "can this book finish faster?" The plot was so predictable and frustrating, and it was <b>
  <i>just.</i>
</b><br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Okay, so it seems that throughout this entire series, whenever there was a need for a villain character, Jeb would come into play, and just show up out of nowhere. It didn't matter how many fricken times he already died, he would come back to life just to be the main antagonist <i>again</i>.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1407437675ra/10719530.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Also, it seemed like James Patterson didn't take death seriously. I mean, if someone died, they was no possibility of them staying dead. Like when Dylan "died" in this book I literally rolled my eyes and said "yeah right". Also, I knew there was no way the flock was actually dead. Even when Fang "died", there was of course a loophole to bring him to life. This is what frustrates me the most... Obviously I don't want them dead, but when you say that someone's dead, can you at least keep them dead? <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380433948ra/873617.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>And don't even get me started with Max and Fang's baby. You're kidding right?? Okay so we got a completely vague description of Fang and Max "doing the do", and I don't even think James Patterson could make it more ill-defined if he <i>tried to.</i> I actually read a spoiler about Max being pregnant with Fang's baby, but <i>i thought it was a <b>joke.</b></i> and doesn't it bother ANYONE that both Max and Fang were barely fifteen? I mean I guess they really did find their soul mate, but I just thought it was a joke. Idk. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>I feel like this book was just an unnecessary installment into this series, and I feel like James Patterson could've fixed up the problems with Nevermore in maybe 100 pages and just released a short story. Everyone seems to be praising this book, and it seems that I'm the only one with an unpopular opinion...<br><span>[image error]</span><br>Felt like this series had so much more potential... but yeah.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="15351347102725648297" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1017071022" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1017071022" />
    <a title="Victoria" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2299764-victoria"><img alt="Victoria" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1242771111p2/2299764.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1017071022?book_show_action=true">Aug 04, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Victoria" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Victoria" href="/user/show/2299764-victoria">Victoria</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1017071022" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3159690135864008235">It is my deep and fervent hope that this is the actual <i>last</i> Maximum Ride book that will come out; even if it is not, I'm pretty certain it's the last one I'll ever read. I guess everyone is forced to have that painful experience at least once in their life where they watch as a beloved book, show, or movie series spirals into mediocrity, so I can now say that this is mine.<br/><br/>This is the story of Max and the Flock after the end of the world that was so abruptly, unbelievably, and unsatisfyingly brou</span>
  <span id="freeText3159690135864008235" style="display:none">It is my deep and fervent hope that this is the actual <i>last</i> Maximum Ride book that will come out; even if it is not, I'm pretty certain it's the last one I'll ever read. I guess everyone is forced to have that painful experience at least once in their life where they watch as a beloved book, show, or movie series spirals into mediocrity, so I can now say that this is mine.<br /><br />This is the story of Max and the Flock after the end of the world that was so abruptly, unbelievably, and unsatisfyingly brought about out of left field at the end of <i>Nevermore</i>. While I guess I was somewhat pleased that Patterson (or whoever actually writes these now) realized what a dumb place to leave a series that was, this book didn't really make things much better.<br /><br />Once again, the character humor that made the first three books instant favorites of mine was practically nil. Most of the book is a depressing, repetitive scan of what remains of the world, which is not much. Over and over again the reader is hit with international scenes of death, starvation, plague, nuclear fallout; basically literally every apocalyptic dystopian scenario happened <i>at the same time</i>. We see and are told about what various disasters and mass death befell each major country and city. It very nearly bypasses grimdark and goes straight into laughable. Either way, it's just entirely the wrong tone for what started out as an action-y sci-fi series with a strong sense of humor and fun. Character interactions aren't much better; most of it is fighting, grieving, and angsting, internally and externally.<br /><br />Pretty much every ounce of conflict is just a rehashing and recombining of previous book issues, which makes them tiresome on top of nonsensical since you just know you've read all these scenarios already. Tension with Angel. Guilt and tension over Dylan. Is Fang going to die? Which crazy groups want to end humanity now? Will the Flock break up? Who's behind everything? Etc., etc. <br /><br />I also <i>seriously</i> facepalmed at <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Max's pregnancy. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> All along James Patterson has stuck those disclaimers at the front of the books regarding his previous 'adult' bird-kid duality <i>When the Wind Blows</i> and <i>The Lake House</i>, and what does he do at the eleventh hour? Stick in one of the only major remaining plot points in which the two differed. The sad thing is, he did it <i>better</i> in the older two novels; it made more sense, was less out of left field, had much less edge of squick, and <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Max and Ozymandias (Fang)'s love scene in The Lake House was actually tender and emotional and took up three-plus chapters instead of three sentences. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Also, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Dylan the plot tumor is FINALLY out of the picture, but even that was cliche and unsatisfying and utterly last minute, so I can barely feel pleased about it <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. <br /><br />There is pretty much only one thing that made this book even the slightest bit worth reading and saved it from a one-star. It's that the ending was happy (if cheesy, yes), concrete, and gave me the bittersweet peace of mind that I could at least leave the Flock in a better place than the awful, stupid close of <i>Nevermore.</i><br /><br />Still should have ended with book three. Now for the love I bear the Flock, <i>let it rest</i>, JP.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3159690135864008235" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1109073606" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1109073606" />
    <a title="Hannah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30909158-hannah"><img alt="Hannah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1437012192p2/30909158.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1109073606?book_show_action=true">Nov 17, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hannah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hannah" href="/user/show/30909158-hannah">Hannah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1109073606" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18058207950250546499">SPOILERS.<br/>This book was terrible. After the gut wrenching blow from "Nevermore" I figured it couldn't end any worse. But at least it was the ending! Finally, after trails and error I made it, and felt a wave of relief.<br/> <br/> I'm sorry, but- you know what? Scratch that, I'm not sorry. The whole thing made me furious. It left me with millions of questions that I couldn't stand. Then a beacon of hope. ANOTHER BOOK!!! The hopes that this book would clear everything up and make me feel so much better were </span>
  <span id="freeText18058207950250546499" style="display:none">SPOILERS.<br />This book was terrible. After the gut wrenching blow from "Nevermore" I figured it couldn't end any worse. But at least it was the ending! Finally, after trails and error I made it, and felt a wave of relief.<br /> <br /> I'm sorry, but- you know what? Scratch that, I'm not sorry. The whole thing made me furious. It left me with millions of questions that I couldn't stand. Then a beacon of hope. ANOTHER BOOK!!! The hopes that this book would clear everything up and make me feel so much better were at a large. An ending that was satisfactory, but has some sacrifice. <br />HAHA NOPE.<br /><br />What I REALLY don't wants to read about is a stupid on-off love story about Max and Fang when all he ends up doing is hurting her and all she ends up doing is crying "so hard she thinks she's going to puke" (and sometimes she does!!) That's gross, and completely unnecessary. <br /><br />I hated the teenage drama and how Nudge, Gazzy and Iggy were all of a sudden jerked into the story. Angels constant on/off evil and deception was completely traumatizing. Please, get your characters straight. <br /><br />And the thing that really disturbed me? Max getting pregnant with Fangs child. Dis. Gust. Ing. DISGUSTING. You read right! Pregnant at age 15. Disconnected and unhealthy. When writing a young adult book, DO NOT put in the message that it is in any way okay to get pregnant at 15. The message that sends is revolting. <br /><br /> The deaths and gruesome descriptions were unnecessary. Just calm down the gore. And how, did those rabid, huge dogs get into the 30th story of a skyscraper to attack the flock?! While the whole city was flooded? That was never explained.<br /> So in total my problems in a nutshell:<br /><br />-Max being a blubbering mess constantly<br />-Angels on/off evil<br />-Dylan being the only Horseman going after Fang<br />-The unnecessary gore just for show<br />-What the heck is Harry's character?!!<br />-The cryenas suddenly appear on the 30th floor <br />- The fake deaths<br />-The in and out into the plot of many characters. They just come in and out of the story and it's weird!<br />- Dylan's sacrifice for Max<br />- ^^ how she spent "years to get over it"<br />- MAX GETTING FREAKING PREGNANT<br />- Max being a teenager <br />- Fang always leaving for her "protection" when all it does is make her throw up in sadness.<br />-DR GUNTHER HAGEN? Why did he have to be the evil guy? He wasn't even on my mind through the series.<br />-the unhealthy relationship between not only Max and Fang but THE WHOLE FLOCK!!! <br />-The constant uncomfortable love triangle.<br />- How COMPLETELY RIGHT Nudge was when she says<br />How "Max just won't be able to live without someone fighting over her"<br />- Max's mother and sisters deaths.<br />- The random tribe of fish people....?<br />- Max letting the apocalypse happen while worrying about Fang and Dylan.<br />- How does Dylan sacrifice himself? Electrocuting yourself saves Fang....? <br />- Max not getting over Dylan EVEN though he died for the person she had a baby with. Fang is the one she loved and yet she's still not happy. She becomes sad about Dylan. She can't make up her mind and I wanted to slap her in the face. <br />-Deaths<br />- So much death<br />- disgusting "it's okay to have a baby at age 15!!" <br />- The cliché name of their baby <br />"PHOENIX"<br />- because she "gives them light in the dark" and "she has wings" (duh...) <br />- Fang laughs now... "Chuckles" and is all "We won't EVER let you fall!"<br />Just stop the cliché act okay?<br /><br />A TOTAL disappointment to me and all the flock lovers out there. I loved the first three books. Then it all started to go down the drain. This was extremely upsetting.</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">

<span id="freeTextContainer848382655806744990">I freaking hated this, the ending and everything. Spoiler: Maximum's pregnant with Fang's baby, no, unfortunately, I didn't make that up.   <span id="freeText848382655806744990" style="display:none">I freaking hated this, the ending and everything. Spoiler: Maximum's pregnant with Fang's baby, no, unfortunately, I didn't make that up. It really bothers me that in past books we found Fang came from teenage parents and he repeated that, fulfilling a boring statistic. What pisses me off the most though is the idea that someone can be programmed to love someone and only that someone forever. Dylan was my favorite in all of this, he was my one good thing in this whole freaking catastrophe and then he offed himself for Fang, a half of a relationship I never even freaking cared about. Maximum and Fang were Ross and Rachel for me: get together, don't get together, I lost interest a long time ago. The fact Dylan could never grow to love someone as much as he loved Maximum is ridiculous to me. It just pisses me off. To me the heart is the strolling bada** of the human anatomy, and it can do whatever the heck it wants, but no - Dylan will forever be devoted to her - and that is some major BS for me. Screw that idea and screw this ending. <br />Also, this is more general, not a fault found only in this book. I'm tired of all YA fiction depicting teenage sex as if it's completely okay if you're in love. Most of these characters are 15-18 (in this case 15 which is disgusting. How can people be happy with this ending? It's ridiculous to assume all they've been through makes them adults), with their full lives ahead of them - they don't know themselves completely yet, they haven't come into their own. How can you just have sex whenever love is thrown in? They should wait to experience more, to know for sure. I hate this so much, I'm just done with this completely. Authors should stop promoting this as if it's completely okay. They can write anything - how about an ideal world? They could even make it seem real and not some parent ploy. <br />Maximum Ride, an Human-Avian hybrid, is a teenage mom - great! Fantastic! I love it! Just kill me, it was a struggle to get through the last part of that book after Dylan's sacrifice. This book completely slaughtered any love I had for this series, which is a shame because I used to love it. This is the worst ending I never could have seen coming - I'd rather have them lose, not be able to save the world, and all die than have to live with this ending. Someone grab the gasoline and a match, light me up like Fall Out Boy! JK, I'm just going to erase all of this awful disaster and try not to stab something. You can't destroy library books, but you can bang them against your bed as much as you want, right? </span>

<div id="review_1264604041" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1264604041" />
    <a title="Milo " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6106947-milo"><img alt="Milo " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1587052645p2/6106947.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1264604041?book_show_action=true">Apr 26, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Milo " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Milo " href="/user/show/6106947-milo">Milo </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780099567486" href="/book/show/23347015-maximum-ride-forever">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6106947-milo?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6106947-milo?shelf=notable-2015-releases">notable-2015-releases</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6106947-milo?shelf=2015-releases-read">2015-releases-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1264604041" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8363375381017010780"><b> <a href='https://thefictionalhangoutsite.wordpress.com/2016/01/18/maximum-ride-9-maximum-ride-forever-by-james-patterson-little-brown-and-comapny//' rel='nofollow noopener'>THE REVIEW CAN ALSO BE FOUND HERE!</a></b><br/><br/>James Patterson’s <i>Maximum Ride</i> series used to be one of my favourite books when I was younger and would always be appointment reading for me, as in, when the new book came out I’d get on that and drop whatever I was currently reading at the moment. However, after the third book, the series started to decrease in quality dramatically, falling into the love triangle plot that is common with so many young adult series nowadays, and as a result, pretty much all the</span>
  <span id="freeText8363375381017010780" style="display:none"><b> <a href="https://thefictionalhangoutsite.wordpress.com/2016/01/18/maximum-ride-9-maximum-ride-forever-by-james-patterson-little-brown-and-comapny//" rel="nofollow noopener">THE REVIEW CAN ALSO BE FOUND HERE!</a></b><br /><br />James Patterson’s <i>Maximum Ride</i> series used to be one of my favourite books when I was younger and would always be appointment reading for me, as in, when the new book came out I’d get on that and drop whatever I was currently reading at the moment. However, after the third book, the series started to decrease in quality dramatically, falling into the love triangle plot that is common with so many young adult series nowadays, and as a result, pretty much all the books after <i>Saving the World (And Other Extreme Sports)</i> (Remember how much better the titles seemed to be before he started naming them after the characters?) aside from <i>Max</i> were a disappointment for me, with <i>Fang</i>, <i>Angel</i> and <i>Nevermore</i> being an example of Patterson at his worst, and the ending to <i>Nevermore</i> was a resounding disappointment. The characters stopped being interesting and likeable, and as a result, my interest in the series wained. However, when <i>Maximum Ride Forever</i> was announced, I was taken by surprise, mainly because <i>Nevermore</i> had been proclaimed to be the last in the series. Evidently Patterson had a change of heart and decided to write another.<br /><br />Luckily, <i>Maximum Ride Forever</i> almost feels like an apology for the terrible <i>Nevermore</i>. It’s what the series finale should have been, wrapping up loose ends, injecting that same tension and pace that the series had in those early days, and gave us a satisfactory conclusion as it looked at life for Max and her flock in a post apocalyptic world that they failed to save. Not many young adult books end with the main protagonists actually losing so this was an interesting development, and Patterson handled this downer ending well, with the usual short chapters and intense pace that comes with his books.<br /><br />The book doesn’t hold back and there are plenty of deaths throughout the book. Eventually not everything is as it seems as Patterson has a habit of bringing characters, both good and evil back from the dead in this series, but the impact is felt. There’s echoes of Patterson’s original duology featuring a winged character that is also named Max but bears little similarity to the character here in the how the book found its resolution, <i>Where the Wind Blows</i> and <i>The Lake House</i> (both of which, in my opinion, show the author at the top of his game), but that’s all there are, echoes. Most of <i>Maximum Ride Forever</i> feels fresh (despite retreading some familiar ground), exciting and Patterson back at his best in the young adult genre.<br /><br />You’ll get through this book pretty quickly as per usual with Patterson books thanks to his trademark style as he gives a satisfactory conclusion to the characters. The characters are handled well for the most part. Even though the attention is focused primarily on Max and Fang as per usual, Nudge, Iggy and the other members of the Flock get more to do here than they’ve had to do in the most recent books from what I can remember, even if their roles have been dramatically reduced since the start of the first book.<br /><br />A few characters aren’t quite as handled well as others, Jeb Batchelder is just kind of there for example because Patterson decided he should be, and Patterson struggles to make us care for the youngest member of the Flock, Angel, who has always been hard to figure out what her role in everything is. There’s an epilogue that ends on a bittersweet note, but for the most part, <i>Maximum Ride Forever</i> serves as a nice swansong for the series and I hope for once Patterson doesn’t decide to return anymore. A spinoff would probably be the best idea at this point, but <i>Maximum Ride Forever</i> is at least, despite a few problems here and there, a good finale that redeems the series from the mess that was <i>Nevermore</i>. For all the freshness that comes with the book however it does revert to a few same old tropes with the love triangle being unfortunately one of the most unwelcome ones, but now, we finally have answers, and more importantly, a proper ending.<br /><br />Fans who have stuck with this series for this long will most likely be rewarded. But I really, really hope there isn’t another entry in this series unless Patterson decides to write his best novel yet, because anything else would probably be a disappointment.<br /><br /><b>VERDICT</b>: 8/10<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8363375381017010780" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1267977710" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1267977710" />
    <a title="Matt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5903843-matt"><img alt="Matt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603562140p2/5903843.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1267977710?book_show_action=true">Apr 30, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Matt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Matt" href="/user/show/5903843-matt">Matt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5903843-matt?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1267977710" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11835620168137612829">In the promised final chapter of the Maximum Ride series, Patterson keeps the reader's curiosity on a sloe boil. Living on a post-apocalyptic earth, Max and her Flock seek to determine if there is anything salvageable. Devastation is rampant and the last documented images from the world's largest cities stream in through a poorly defined 5G network. In order to properly ascertain the answers they seek, the Flock divides and promises to report in as soon as they can. Meanwhile, the Doomsday Cult,</span>
  <span id="freeText11835620168137612829" style="display:none">In the promised final chapter of the Maximum Ride series, Patterson keeps the reader's curiosity on a sloe boil. Living on a post-apocalyptic earth, Max and her Flock seek to determine if there is anything salvageable. Devastation is rampant and the last documented images from the world's largest cities stream in through a poorly defined 5G network. In order to properly ascertain the answers they seek, the Flock divides and promises to report in as soon as they can. Meanwhile, the Doomsday Cult, cloned bird children, lurks in the shadows to snuff out the Flock alongside most of humankind, leaving each Flock member to dodge attempts on their lives with every turn, some with less than successful results. The more Max learns of the situation on earth, the less she seems motivated to trudge on, but she must, as pockets of life emerges throughout her discoveries. The question remains, is the end inevitable, or is there a shimmering ray of light in this overly bleak world? In a fitting ending to the series, Patterson offers his young adult readers a glimpse of the world to come and the way those who witness it react to the final days. Now, can we be sure that Patterson will actually end it here? Let's hope!<br /><br />I got interested in the series years ago, when it was in its early stages. While I am not a 'Young Adult', my dedication to this series offers me some insight to comment on its content, which has unfortunately (but predictably) suffered from PATTERSON SYNDROME. Those familiar with my reviews of James Patterson will know this refers to his desire to churn out drivel, using his name to sell books rather than solid content. The series had some great potential, but lost its lustre and moved into a world of utter cheesiness. Are young adult readers expected to subject themselves to this? I know John Grisham and Kathy Reichs (both having carved out greatness in their adult genre books) have been able to successfully transition without getting too silly. Alas, Patterson lauds himself as an expert, but fails. Also, interesting to see how Patterson climbs up on his soap box and points the finger at Russia, but stops short at referring to Putin when making his case for those who are to blame for the apocalyptic world in which the story takes place. Well played, Mr. P., as you indoctrinate the next generation.<br /><br />Tepid, Mr. Patterson. You seem to want your young readers to stifle their reading abilities and comprehension with this sub-par piece of work.<br /><br />Like/hate the review? An ever-growing collection of others appears at: <br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://pecheyponderings.wordpress.com/">http://pecheyponderings.wordpress.com/</a><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11835620168137612829" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText15697176158415108065" style="display:none">Why, Mr. Patterson, why?<br /><br />I enjoyed 'When the Wind Blows' and 'Lake House', which presented the story of the Angel Experiment children in a much more logical, sane (and better-written) manner than this 'Maximum Ride' drivel. <span id="freeTextContainer4144882209387029225">I read Nevermore back in 6th grade (probably 2012). I was really excited for the *ahem "last book" to come out. <br/><br/>I thought it was the end.<br/><br/>The end.<br/><br/>THE end.<br/><br/>THE END.<br/><br/>But wait, fellow good readers. <b>Apparently not.</b><br/><br/><br/><br/>Life goes on and on. Now I am in 2015. And I see THIS 9th book advertising that it is THE last book. <br/>I went and checked several sources before I wrote this.<br/>My opinions:<br/><br/>Nevermore ended with an ending that I just wanted to scream at the author for. Not because it was good. Because it didn't mak</span>
  <span id="freeText4144882209387029225" style="display:none">I read Nevermore back in 6th grade (probably 2012). I was really excited for the *ahem "last book" to come out. <br /><br />I thought it was the end.<br /><br />The end.<br /><br />THE end.<br /><br />THE END.<br /><br />But wait, fellow good readers. <b>Apparently not.</b><br /><br /><br /><br />Life goes on and on. Now I am in 2015. And I see THIS 9th book advertising that it is THE last book. <br />I went and checked several sources before I wrote this.<br />My opinions:<br /><br />Nevermore ended with an ending that I just wanted to scream at the author for. Not because it was good. Because it didn't make sense and it totally made me go like ????<br /><br />James Patterson, I thought your books were really good. For like the first four books.<br />Then comes cliche plots, love triangles, the ever most evil Angel, and absolutely no voice from all the other characters. Oh, and that ending. <br /><br /><i>So.</i> <b>Cliche</b>. &lt;---- Might as well be my favorite word.<br /><br />What happened to the rest of the flock? Max wasn't supposed to be the only important character here. To me, they're all important.<br />Gazzy.<br />Iggy.<br />Nudge.<br />Ella.<br /><br />What the fucking hell did you put them in?<br /><br /><br />Now, as James Patterson struck a nerve and decides to write the FINAL ending to the series, I will be here whacking my head. <br /><br />Please, please, make up your mind before you decide to do anything with your series. Stick with your original plan, Patterson. Just because you wrote so many books doesn't mean you are a immortal fandom. <br /><u>Let me tell you this, brother. We make up your fans.</u><br /><br /><br />Yeah, I'm still reading it. Maybe at BN for free or the library. Just to see if Patterson at least made a somewhat acceptable ending.<br /><br />Anyone read the first 5 chapters (it literally was 3 because of all the shit there) on his website?</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('dQtNk7bEeq4fFNWPMo48ppos83X3YNJyZiy/L3cBAI5n7TB6y+fzl23eCJ57GNXDRiTdncPD63xROV1+w7xHIg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('EEzzJ8zCgNbXBe1lu8hujdt4fUK04rfhkurI94f6VzACqo7OseEJ76XPMHTyXofoB3BTqoBBju+l/yqmM0cQnA==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer612324268803222272"><a href='http://www.jamespatterson.com' rel='nofollow noopener'>Official US Site</a><br/><a href='http://www.jamespatterson.co.uk' rel='nofollow noopener'>Official UK Site</a><br/><a href='http://jimmypatterson.org' rel='nofollow noopener'>JIMMY Patterson Books</a><br/><a href='http://readkiddoread.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>ReadKiddoRead</a><br/><br/><br/><br/>James Patterson is the world’s bestselling author and most trusted storyteller. He has created more enduring fictional characters than any other novelist writing today, with his Alex Cross, Michael Bennett, Women’s Murder Club, Private, NYPD Red, Daniel X, Maximum Ride, and Middle School series. He has sold over 380 million books wo</span>
  <span id="freeText612324268803222272" style="display:none"><a href="http://www.jamespatterson.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Official US Site</a><br /><a href="http://www.jamespatterson.co.uk" rel="nofollow noopener">Official UK Site</a><br /><a href="http://jimmypatterson.org" rel="nofollow noopener">JIMMY Patterson Books</a><br /><a href="http://readkiddoread.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">ReadKiddoRead</a><br /><br /><br /><br />James Patterson is the world’s bestselling author and most trusted storyteller. He has created more enduring fictional characters than any other novelist writing today, with his Alex Cross, Michael Bennett, Women’s Murder Club, Private, NYPD Red, Daniel X, Maximum Ride, and Middle School series. He has sold over 380 million books worldwide and currently holds the Guinness World Record for the most #1 New York Times bestsellers. In addition to writing the thriller novels for which he is best known, among them The President Is Missing with President Bill Clinton, Patterson also writes fiction for young readers of all ages, including the Max Einstein series, produced in partnership with the Albert Einstein Estate. He is also the first author to have #1 new titles simultaneously on the New York Times adult and children’s bestseller lists.<br /> <br />The son of an insurance salesman and a schoolteacher, Patterson grew up in Newburgh, New York, and began casually writing at the age of nineteen. In 1969, he graduated from Manhattan College. He was given a full-ride scholarship to Vanderbilt University’s graduate program in English. He left Vanderbilt before getting his PhD due to complications involving the Vietnam War. <br /> <br />Instead, he moved to New York to become a junior copywriter for the advertising agency J. Walter Thompson, eventually becoming CEO of its North American company.<br /> <br />In 1976, while still working for J. Walter Thompson, Patterson published his first novel, The Thomas Berryman Number, with Little, Brown and Company. After being turned down by thirty-one publishers, it won the Edgar Award for Best First Novel. Patterson’s 1993 novel, Along Came a Spider, his first book to feature Alex Cross, was also his first New York Times bestseller in fiction.<br /> <br />In 2001, Morgan Freeman starred as Alex Cross in a film adaptation of Along Came a Spider, and Tyler Perry also played the character in the 2012 film Alex Cross. A film adaptation of Patterson’s middle-grade novel Middle School: The Worst Years of My Life was released in theaters in October 2016.<br /> <br />James Patterson has donated more than one million books to students, focusing on some of the most under-resourced schools and youth programs in the country. To date, he has donated $7.25 million to school and classroom libraries throughout the United States, and $2.1 million to independent bookstores and employees.<br /> <br />Patterson has recently donated over $35 million to his and his wife’s alma maters—the University of Wisconsin, Vanderbilt University, and Manhattan College—and he has established over four hundred Teacher and Writer Education Scholarships at twenty-one colleges and universities throughout the country. Patterson has also donated more than one million books to U.S. soldiers at home and overseas.<br /> <br />In May 2015, Patterson launched a children’s book imprint at Little, Brown—JIMMY Patterson—that is unwaveringly focused on one goal: turning kids into lifelong readers. This imprint also provides resources, strategies, and programs to serve teachers, parents, librarians, and booksellers. Patterson invests proceeds from the sales of JIMMY Patterson Books in pro-reading initiatives.<br /> <br />Patterson also founded ReadKiddoRead.com, a website designed to help parents, teachers, and librarians ignite a new generation’s excitement for reading. Awarded the National Book Foundation’s Innovations in Reading Prize and the American Library Association’s Great Websites for Kids, the site features thoughtful book reviews from a variety of genres and age ranges, a large and lively Facebook community, and contributions from other authors.<br /> <br />Patterson’s awards for adult and children’s literature include the Edgar Award, the International </span>
